href="/wiki/Countries_of_the_United_Kingdom_by_GVA_per_capita" title="Countries of the United Kingdom by GVA per capita">5th</a>)</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/NUTS_statistical_regions_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="NUTS statistical regions of the United Kingdom">NUTS code</a></th><td>\nUKF</td></tr><tr class="mergedrow"><th scope="row"><a href="/wiki/ONS_coding_system" title="ONS coding system">ONS code</a></th><td>\nE12000004</td></tr><tr class="mergedtoprow"><th scope="row">Website</th><td>\n<span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.emcouncils.gov.uk/Home">www<wbr />.emcouncils<wbr />.gov<wbr />.uk<wbr />/Home</a></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>East Midlands</b> is one of nine official <a href="/wiki/Regions_of_England" title="Regions of England">regions of England</a> at the <a href="/wiki/First_level_NUTS_of_the_European_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="First level NUTS of the European Union">first level of NUTS</a> for <a href="/wiki/Eurostat" title="Eurostat">statistical</a> purposes. It consists of <a href="/wiki/Derbyshire" title="Derbyshire">Derbyshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leicestershire" title="Leicestershire">Leicestershire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire" title="Lincolnshire">Lincolnshire</a> (except <a href="/wiki/Northern_Lincolnshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Northern Lincolnshire">North</a> and <a href="/wiki/North_East_Lincolnshire" title="North East Lincolnshire">North East Lincolnshire</a>), <a href="/wiki/Northamptonshire" title="Northamptonshire">Northamptonshire</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nottinghamshire" title="Nottinghamshire">Nottinghamshire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rutland" title="Rutland">Rutland</a>. The region has an area of 15,627&#160;km<sup>2</sup> (6,034&#160;sq&#160;mi), with a population over 4.5&#160;million in 2011. There are five main urban centres, <a href="/wiki/Derby,_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Derby, England">Derby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Leicester" title="Leicester">Leicester</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lincoln,_England" title="Lincoln, England">Lincoln</a>, <a href="/wiki/Northampton" title="Northampton">Northampton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nottingham,_England" class="mw-redirect" title="Nottingham, England">Nottingham</a>. Others include <a href="/wiki/Boston,_Lincolnshire" title="Boston, Lincolnshire">Boston</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chesterfield,_Derbyshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Chesterfield, Derbyshire">Chesterfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Corby,_Northamptonshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Corby, Northamptonshire">Corby</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grantham,_Lincolnshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Grantham, Lincolnshire">Grantham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hinckley,_Leicestershire" class="mw-redirect" title="Hinckley, Leicestershire">Hinckley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kettering,_Northamptonshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Kettering, Northamptonshire">Kettering</a>, <a href="/wiki/Loughborough" title="Loughborough">Loughborough</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mansfield,_Nottinghamshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Mansfield, Nottinghamshire">Mansfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Newark-on-Trent" title="Newark-on-Trent">Newark-on-Trent</a>  and <a href="/wiki/Wellingborough,_Northamptonshire" class="mw-redirect" title="Wellingborough, Northamptonshire">Wellingborough</a>. Relative proximity to London and its position on the national motorway and trunk road networks help the East Midlands to thrive as an economic hub. <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Airport" title="East Midlands Airport">East Midlands Airport</a>, 18 miles (29&#160;km) from Leicester, is between Derby, Loughborough and Nottingham.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" class="toctext">High technology</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-36"><a href="#Finance"><span class="tocnumber">9.8</span> <span class="toctext">Finance</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-37"><a href="#Rural"><span class="tocnumber">9.9</span> <span class="toctext">Rural</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-38"><a href="#Entertainment"><span class="tocnumber">9.10</span> <span class="toctext">Entertainment</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-39"><a href="#Education"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">Education</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-40"><a href="#Secondary_education"><span class="tocnumber">10.1</span> <span class="toctext">Secondary education</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-41"><a href="#Top_twenty_state_schools_in_the_East_Midlands_(2015_A-level_results)"><span class="tocnumber">10.2</span> <span class="toctext">Top twenty state schools in the East Midlands (2015 A-level results)</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-42"><a href="#Universities"><span class="tocnumber">10.3</span> <span class="toctext">Universities</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-43"><a href="#Sports"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Sports</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-44"><a href="#Football"><span class="tocnumber">11.1</span> <span class="toctext">Football</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-45"><a href="#Rugby_Union"><span class="tocnumber">11.2</span> <span class="toctext">Rugby Union</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-46"><a href="#Cricket"><span class="tocnumber">11.3</span> <span class="toctext">Cricket</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-47"><a href="#Basketball"><span class="tocnumber">11.4</span> <span class="toctext">Basketball</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-48"><a href="#Motor_sports"><span class="tocnumber">11.5</span> <span class="toctext">Motor sports</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-49"><a href="#Swimming"><span class="tocnumber">11.6</span> <span class="toctext">Swimming</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-50"><a href="#Local_media"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">Local media</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-51"><a href="#Television"><span class="tocnumber">12.1</span> <span class="toctext">Television</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-52"><a href="#Radio"><span class="tocnumber">12.2</span> <span class="toctext">Radio</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-53"><a href="#Newspapers"><span class="tocnumber">12.3</span> <span class="toctext">Newspapers</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-54"><a href="#Magazines"><span class="tocnumber">12.4</span> <span class="toctext">Magazines</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-55"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">13</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-56"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">14</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-57"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">15</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Midlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The high point at 636&#160;m (2,087&#160;ft) is <a href="/wiki/Kinder_Scout" title="Kinder Scout">Kinder Scout</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Peak_District" title="Peak District">Peak District</a> of the southern <a href="/wiki/Pennines" title="Pennines">Pennines</a> in northwest <a href="/wiki/Derbyshire" title="Derbyshire">Derbyshire</a> near <a href="/wiki/Glossop" title="Glossop">Glossop</a>. Other upland, hilly areas of 95 to 280&#160;m (312 to 919&#160;ft) in altitude, together with lakes and reservoirs, rise in and around the <a href="/wiki/Charnwood_Forest" title="Charnwood Forest">Charnwood Forest</a> north of <a href="/wiki/Leicester" title="Leicester">Leicester</a>, and in the <a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire_Wolds" title="Lincolnshire Wolds">Lincolnshire Wolds</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The region\'s major rivers, the <a href="/wiki/River_Nene" title="River Nene">Nene</a>, the <a href="/wiki/River_Soar" title="River Soar">Soar</a>, the <a href="/wiki/River_Trent" title="River Trent">Trent</a> and the <a href="/wiki/River_Welland" title="River Welland">Welland</a>, flow in a northeasterly direction towards the <a href="/wiki/Humber" title="Humber">Humber</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Wash" title="The Wash">the Wash</a>. The <a href="/wiki/River_Derwent,_Derbyshire" title="River Derwent, Derbyshire">Derwent</a>, conversely, rises in the High Peak before flowing south to join the Trent some 2 miles (3&#160;km) before its conflux with the Soar.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Forbidding_Office_Building_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1363225.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Forbidding_Office_Building_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1363225.jpg/220px-Forbidding_Office_Building_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1363225.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Forbidding_Office_Building_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1363225.jpg/330px-Forbidding_Office_Building_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1363225.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Forbidding_Office_Building_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1363225.jpg/440px-Forbidding_Office_Building_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1363225.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Forbidding_Office_Building_-_geograph.org.uk_-_1363225.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Royal Society of Wildlife Trusts, next to the Trent, and Waitrose, in Newark-on-Trent</div></div></div>\n<p>The centre of the East Midlands area lies roughly between <a href="/wiki/Bingham,_Nottinghamshire" title="Bingham, Nottinghamshire">Bingham</a>, Nottinghamshire and <a href="/wiki/Bottesford,_Leicestershire" title="Bottesford, Leicestershire">Bottesford</a>, Leicestershire. The <a href="/wiki/Centre_points_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Centre points of the United Kingdom">geographical centre of England</a> lies in <a href="/wiki/Higham_on_the_Hill" title="Higham on the Hill">Higham on the Hill</a> in west <a href="/wiki/Leicestershire" title="Leicestershire">Leicestershire</a>, close to the boundary between the Leicestershire and Warwickshire. Some 88 per cent of the land is rural in character, although agriculture accounts for less than three per cent of the region\'s jobs.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire" title="Lincolnshire">Lincolnshire</a> is the only maritime county of the six, with a true North Sea coastline of about 30 miles (48&#160;km) due to the protection afforded by Spurn Head and the North Norfolk foreshore.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Church Flatts Farm in <a href="/wiki/Coton_in_the_Elms" title="Coton in the Elms">Coton in the Elms</a>, South Derbyshire, is the furthest place from the sea in the UK (70 miles, 110&#160;km). In April 1936 the first <a href="/wiki/Ordnance_Survey" title="Ordnance Survey">Ordnance Survey</a> <a href="/wiki/Triangulation_station" title="Triangulation station">trig point</a> was sited at <a href="/wiki/Cold_Ashby" title="Cold Ashby">Cold Ashby</a> in Northamptonshire.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Royal_Society_of_Wildlife_Trusts" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Society of Wildlife Trusts">Royal Society of Wildlife Trusts</a> and <a href="/wiki/The_Wildlife_Trusts" title="The Wildlife Trusts">The Wildlife Trusts</a> are based next to the River Trent and Newark Castle railway station. The <a href="/wiki/National_Centre_for_Earth_Observation" title="National Centre for Earth Observation">National Centre for Earth Observation</a> is at the University of Leicester.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Midlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The region is home to large quantities of <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Oil_Province" title="East Midlands Oil Province">East Midlands Oil Province</a>. <a href="/wiki/Charnwood_Forest" title="Charnwood Forest">Charnwood Forest</a> is noted for its abundant levels of volcanic rock, estimated to be approximately 600 million years old.<sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A quarter of the UK\'s <a href="/wiki/Cement" title="Cement">cement</a> is manufactured in the region, at three sites in <a href="/wiki/Hope,_Derbyshire" title="Hope, Derbyshire">Hope</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tunstead,_Derbyshire" title="Tunstead, Derbyshire">Tunstead</a> in Derbyshire, and <a href="/wiki/Ketton_Cement_Works" title="Ketton Cement Works">Ketton Cement Works</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rutland" title="Rutland">Rutland</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> Of the <a href="/wiki/Construction_aggregate" title="Construction aggregate">aggregates</a> produced in the region, 25 per cent are from Derbyshire and four per cent from Leicestershire. Lincolnshire and Nottinghamshire each produce around 30 per cent of the region\'s <a href="/wiki/Sand_mining" title="Sand mining">sand</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gravel_pit" title="Gravel pit">gravel</a> output.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Barwell" title="Barwell">Barwell</a> in Leicestershire was the site of Britain\'s largest <a href="/wiki/Meteorite" title="Meteorite">meteorite</a> (7&#160;kg, 15&#160;lb) on 24 December 1965. The <a href="/wiki/2008_Lincolnshire_earthquake" class="mw-redirect" title="2008 Lincolnshire earthquake">2008 Lincolnshire earthquake</a> was 5.2 in <a href="/wiki/Moment_magnitude" class="mw-redirect" title="Moment magnitude">magnitude</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Environment">Environment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Midlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Environment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Areas of the East Midlands designated by the East Midlands Biodiversity Partnership as Biodiversity Conservation Areas include:<sup id="cite_ref-Biodiversity_Partnerships_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Biodiversity_Partnerships-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Charnwood_Forest" title="Charnwood Forest">Charnwood Forest</a></li>\n<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Coversand_Heaths&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Coversand Heaths (page does not exist)">Coversand Heaths</a></li>\n<li>Derbyshire Peak Fringe and Lower Derwent</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Humberhead_Levels" title="Humberhead Levels">Humberhead Levels</a></li>\n<li>Leighland Forest</li>\n<li>The Lincolnshire Limewoods and Heaths</li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire_coast" title="Lincolnshire coast">Lincolnshire coast</a></li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Peak_District" title="Peak District">Peak District</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rockingham_Forest" title="Rockingham Forest">Rockingham Forest</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Sherwood_Forest" title="Sherwood Forest">Sherwood Forest</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Rutland" title="Rutland">Rutland</a>, SW <a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire" title="Lincolnshire">Lincolnshire</a> and N <a href="/wiki/Northamptonshire" title="Northamptonshire">Northamptonshire</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/The_Wash" title="The Wash">The Wash</a></li></ul>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Image-Major_Oak_in_Sherwood_Forest_in_2006_(2).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Image-Major_Oak_in_Sherwood_Forest_in_2006_%282%29.jpg/220px-Image-Major_Oak_in_Sherwood_Forest_in_2006_%282%29.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Image-Major_Oak_in_Sherwood_Forest_in_2006_%282%29.jpg/330px-Image-Major_Oak_in_Sherwood_Forest_in_2006_%282%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6a/Image-Major_Oak_in_Sherwood_Forest_in_2006_%282%29.jpg/440px-Image-Major_Oak_in_Sherwood_Forest_in_2006_%282%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Image-Major_Oak_in_Sherwood_Forest_in_2006_(2).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Major_Oak" title="Major Oak">Major Oak</a> in Sherwood Forest; a traditional landmark of the north-east Midlands. The current <a href="/wiki/Sheriff_of_Nottingham" title="Sheriff of Nottingham">Sheriff of Nottingham</a> is Glyn Jenkins<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Areas of the East Midlands designated by the East Midlands Biodiversity Partnership as <a href="/w/index.php?title=Biodiversity_Enhancement_Areas&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Biodiversity Enhancement Areas (page does not exist)">Biodiversity Enhancement Areas</a> include:<sup id="cite_ref-Biodiversity_Partnerships_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Biodiversity_Partnerships-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Coalfields" class="mw-redirect" title="Coalfields">Coalfields</a></li>\n<li>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Daventry_Grasslands&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Daventry Grasslands (page does not exist)">Daventry Grasslands</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/The_Fens" title="The Fens">The Fens</a></li>\n<li>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Lincolnshire_Coastal_Grazing_Marshes&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Lincolnshire Coastal Grazing Marshes (page does not exist)">Lincolnshire Coastal Grazing Marshes</a></li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire_Wolds" title="Lincolnshire Wolds">Lincolnshire Wolds</a></li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/National_Forest,_England" class="mw-redirect" title="National Forest, England">National Forest</a></li>\n<li>The <a href="/w/index.php?title=Yardley-Whittlewood_Ridge&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Yardley-Whittlewood Ridge (page does not exist)">Yardley-Whittlewood Ridge</a></li></ul>\n<p>Two of the nationally designated <a href="/wiki/Area_of_Outstanding_Natural_Beauty" title="Area of Outstanding Natural Beauty">Areas of Outstanding Natural Beauty</a> are:<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Peak_District" title="Peak District">Peak District</a></li>\n<li>The <a href="/wiki/Lincolnshire_Wolds" title="Lincolnshire Wolds">Lincolnshire Wolds</a></li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Forestry">Forestry</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Midlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Forestry">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Several towns in the southern part of the region, including Market Harborough, Desborough, Rothwell, Corby, Kettering, Thrapston, Oundle and Stamford, lie within the boundaries of what was once <a href="/wiki/Rockingham_Forest" title="Rockingham Forest">Rockingham Forest</a> \xe2\x80\x93 designated a <a href="/wiki/Royal_forest" title="Royal forest">royal forest</a> by <a href="/wiki/William_the_Conqueror" title="William the Conqueror">William the Conqueror</a> and was long hunted by English kings and queens.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/The_National_Forest_(England)" title="The National Forest (England)">National Forest</a> is an environmental project in central England run by The National Forest Company. Areas of north Leicestershire, south Derbyshire and south-east Staffordshire covering around 200 square miles (520&#160;km<sup>2</sup>; 52,000&#160;ha) are being planted in an attempt to blend ancient woodland with new plantings. It stretches from the western outskirts of Leicester in the east to Burton upon Trent in the west, and is planned to link the ancient forests of Needwood and Charnwood.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (April 2016)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sherwood_Forest" title="Sherwood Forest">Sherwood Forest</a> in Nottinghamshire attracts many visitors, and is perhaps best known for its ties with the legend of <a href="/wiki/Robin_Hood" title="Robin Hood">Robin Hood</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Governance">Governance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Midlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Governance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:United_Kingdom_European_Union_referendum_2016_voting_area_results_(East_Midlands).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/United_Kingdom_European_Union_referendum_2016_voting_area_results_%28East_Midlands%29.svg/220px-United_Kingdom_European_Union_referendum_2016_voting_area_results_%28East_Midlands%29.svg.png" width="220" height="261" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/United_Kingdom_European_Union_referendum_2016_voting_area_results_%28East_Midlands%29.svg/330px-United_Kingdom_European_Union_referendum_2016_voting_area_results_%28East_Midlands%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/United_Kingdom_European_Union_referendum_2016_voting_area_results_%28East_Midlands%29.svg/440px-United_Kingdom_European_Union_referendum_2016_voting_area_results_%28East_Midlands%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1099" data-file-height="1305" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:United_Kingdom_European_Union_referendum_2016_voting_area_results_(East_Midlands).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In the June 2016 <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum,_2016" title="United Kingdom European Union membership referendum, 2016">EU referendum</a>, only Leicester and Rushcliffe had a majorities in favour of Remain, and Boston had the highest proportion of leave voters</div></div></div>\n<p>Regional financial funding decisions for the East Midlands are taken by <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Councils" title="East Midlands Councils">East Midlands Councils</a>, based in <a href="/wiki/Melton_Mowbray" title="Melton Mowbray">Melton Mowbray</a>. East Midlands Councils is an unelected body made up of representatives of local government in the region. The defunct <a href="/wiki/East_Midlands_Development_Agency" title="East Midlands Development Agency">East Midlands Development Agency</a> was headquartered next to the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>\'s East Midlands office in Nottingham and made financial decisions regarding economic development in the region. Since the <a href="/wiki/Cameron-Clegg_coalition" class="mw-redirect" title="Cameron-Clegg coalition">Conservative-Lib Dem coalition government</a> launched its austerity programme after the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_general_election,_2010" title="United Kingdom general election, 2010">2010 general election</a>, regional bodies such as those have been devolved to smaller groups now on a county level. As a region today, there is no overriding body with significant financial or planning powers for the East Midlands.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Population_and_settlement">Population and settlement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=East_Midlands&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Population and settlement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="vertical-navbox vcard" style="float:right;clear:right;width:22.0em;margin:0 0 1.0em 1.0em;background:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;padding:0.2em;border-spacing:0.4em 0;text-align:center;line-height:1.4em;font-size:88%;width:21.0em;"><tbody><tr><th style="padding:0.2em 0.4em 0.2em;font-size:145%;line-height:1.2em"><div class="adr" style="font-size:smaller"><span class="fn org country-name"><a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a></span>\n</div></th></tr><tr><th><a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Arms_of_England.svg" class="image"><img alt="Royal Arms of England.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Royal_Arms_of_England.svg/125px-Royal_Arms_of_England.svg.png" width="125" height="146" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Royal_Arms_of_England.svg/188px-Royal_Arms_of_England.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Royal_Arms_of_England.svg/250px-Royal_Arms_of_England.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="410" data-file-height="478" /></a></th></tr><tr><th
